COSC 102
Description: COSC 102 - Introduction to Computer Science 4 Credit Hours Problem solving+algorithm development. Organization+characteristics of modern digital computers with emphasis on software engineering or building abstractions with procedures+data,+programming in a modern computer language. Includes Level 1 design projects or which require laboratory work. Contact Hour Distribution: 3 hours lecture+1 lab.Grading Restriction: A or B or C or No Credit grading only.Credit Restriction: Students who have received credit for 140 or 160 may not receive subsequent credit for 102 without consent of instructor.(RE) Corequisite(s): Mathematics 141 or 147.
Prerequisites: 
Corequisites: Mathematics 141 or 147

MATH 130
Description: MATH 130 - Precalculus I 4 Credit Hours Review of algebraic or logarithmic or exponential,+trigonometric functions. Grading Restriction: A or B or C or No Credit grading only.Credit Restriction: Students who receive a grade of C or better in 141 or 147 or 151 may not subsequently receive credit for 130.(RE) Prerequisite(s): 119 with a grade of C or better or appropriate placement exam score.Comment(s): For students who satisfy the course prerequisites for 141 or 151 or but whose placement test scores indicate additional preparation is necessary.
Prerequisites: 119 with a grade of C or better or appropriate placement exam score
Corequisites:

Students receiving a passing grade below B in 118 will complete the English Composition requirement by taking 102. Students receiving a grade of B or above will complete their freshman English requirements by choosing 102 or a sophomore-level course in the English Department or 355.

COSC 453
Description: COSC 453 - Data Visualization 3 Credit Hours The goal of this course is to develop a broad understanding of the principles or methods,+techniques for designing effective data visualizations. The course will follow a lecture/seminar style with discussion of assigned readings or as well as viewing of videos+hands-on experience with creating visualization tools. (RE) Prerequisite(s): 140.Recommended Background: 340+452.

ECE 256
Description: ECE 256 - Computer System Interfaces 3 Credit Hours Introduction to design or implementation,+test of interfaces used in the construction of modern computing systems. Topics covered include memory+I/O devices or component interfaces or real-time operating system concepts or performance analysis,+optimizations. The lectures+lab assignments will cover both hardware+software elements needed to support target applications+interfaces. This includes physical layer+low-level protocol/information-format design+analysis. Other key elements covered in the class include direct memory access or timers or input/output synchronization,+interrupts. Emphasis is placed on hands-on+lab based exercises using an appropriate development system. (RE) Prerequisite(s): 255.
Prerequisites: 255
Corequisites:

COSC 425
Description: COSC 425 - Introduction to Machine Learning 3 Credit Hours Machine learning is concerned with computer programs that automatically improve their performance through experience. This course covers the theory+practice of machine learning from a variety of perspectives. We cover topics such as clustering or decision trees or neural network learning or statistical learning methods or Bayesian learning methods or dimension reduction or kernel methods,+reinforcement learning. Programming assignments include implementation+hands-on experiments with various learning algorithms. (RE) Prerequisite(s): Electrical+Computer Engineering 313 or 317 or Mathematics 323; Mathematics 251 or 257.Comment(s): Prior knowledge may satisfy prerequisite with consent of instructor.
Prerequisites: Electrical+Computer Engineering 313 or 317 or Mathematics 323; Mathematics 251 or 257
Corequisites:

Description: COSC 445 - Fundamentals of Digital Archeology 3 Credit Hours This is an advanced topic course focused on developing multi-disciplinary skills of discovering or retrieving or analyzing,+presenting operational data. Students will use critical thinking+intense practice solving real-world problems to recognize+address key operational issues: the lack of context or missing observations,+incorrect values. At the end of the course students will be able to discover operational data or to retrieve+store it or to recover context or to estimate the impact of missing events or to identify unreliable or incorrect values,+to present the results. Recommended Background: 340 or 370 or Electrical+Computer Engineering 313.

The class will introduce basic topics core to understanding computer security including security goals or threat modeling or software security or operating system security or cryptography or network security,+human factors. Coursework focuses on helping students adapt a security aware mindset when designing or developing,+testing systems. Credit Restriction: Cannot receive credit for both ECE 461+COSC 366.(RE) Prerequisite(s): COSC 302 or COSC 307 with a grade of C or better,+either ECE 256 or COSC 230 with a grade of C or better.
Prerequisites: COSC 302 or COSC 307 with a grade of C or better,+either ECE 256 or COSC 230 with a grade of C or better
Corequisites:

COSC 453
Description: COSC 453 - Data Visualization 3 Credit Hours The goal of this course is to develop a broad understanding of the principles or methods,+techniques for designing effective data visualizations. The course will span a wide range of topics related to interactive data visualization. The course will teach key elements of scientific visualization techniques or which graphically encode data with some physical or geometric correspondence,+information visualization techniques or which focus on abstract data without such correspondences such as symbolic or tabular or networked or hierarchical or textual information sources. The course will follow a lecture/seminar style with discussion of assigned readings or as well as viewing of videos+hands-on experience with creating visualization tools. (RE) Prerequisite(s): COSC 140 with a grade of C or better.Recommended Background: COSC 340+COSC 452 .

ECE 256
Description: ECE 256 - Computer System Interfaces 3 Credit Hours Introduction to design or implementation,+test of interfaces used in the construction of modern computing systems. Topics covered include memory+I/O devices or component interfaces or real-time operating system concepts or performance analysis,+optimizations. The lectures+lab assignments will cover both hardware+software elements needed to support target applications+interfaces. This includes physical layer+low-level protocol/information-format design+analysis. Other key elements covered in the class include direct memory access or timers or input/output synchronization,+interrupts. Emphasis is placed on hands-on+lab based exercises using an appropriate development system. (RE) Prerequisite(s): ECE 255 with a grade of C or better.
Prerequisites: ECE 255 with a grade of C or better
Corequisites:

Description: COSC 425 - Introduction to Machine Learning 3 Credit Hours Machine learning is concerned with computer programs that automatically improve their performance through experience. Programming assignments include implementation+hands-on experiments with various learning algorithms. COSC 445
Description: COSC 445 - Fundamentals of Digital Archeology 3 Credit Hours This is an advanced topic course focused on developing multi-disciplinary skills of discovering or retrieving or analyzing,+presenting operational data. Students will use critical thinking+intense practice solving real-world problems to recognize+address key operational issues: the lack of context or missing observations,+incorrect values. At the end of the course students will be able to discover operational data or to retrieve+store it or to recover context or to estimate the impact of missing events or to identify unreliable or incorrect values,+to present the results. Description: ECE 201 - Circuits I 3 Credit Hours Fundamental laws of circuit analysis. Ohm’s Law. Kirchhoff’s current+voltage laws; the law of conservation of energy; circuits containing independent+dependent voltage,+current sources or resistance or conductance or capacitance,+inductance analyzed using mesh+nodal analysis or superposition,+source of transformations;+Norton’s+Thevenin’s Theorems. Steady state analysis of DC+AC circuits. Complete solution for transient analysis for circuits with one+two storage elements. EF 203
Description: EF 203 - Engineering Based Problem Solving 3 Credit Hours The objective is to develop engineering focused critical problem solving skills for undergraduate engineering+business majors. Students are introduced to engineering problems from a systems perspective or allowing students to analyze a range of systems from simple entities to larger more complex systems such as organizations. There are three phases of the critical problem solving skills as exemplified by the DRIVES model. The first phase focuses on defining the right problem. The second phase details a solution based on the concepts of flow or variation,+disruption. The third phase introduces the sustainability of the solution based on the concepts of reliability+the role of culture in design. Alternative solutions will be reviewed from a business perspective. Registration Restriction(s): Sophomore standing.
Prerequisites: 
Corequisites: 

EF 303
Description: EF 303 - Creating Synergies in Business+Engineering Collaborations 3 Credit Hours The objective is to develop the skills+understanding to create effective cross disciplinary engineering+business teams. Students will work to understand the key requirements of projects from both the business+engineering perspective. Additionally or students will be able to apply basic engineering principles in a business context. Scenarios in new product development+operations will be considered. Topics may include identifying needs/key requirements or project management,+sensitivity analysis of solutions from the profit+loss perspective. (RE) Prerequisite(s): EF 203 or consent of instructor.
Prerequisites: EF 203 or consent of instructor

Emphasis on argumentation or critical inquiry or rhetorical analysis,+research methods. May include the study of a long work of literature or nonfiction in addition to a selection of interdisciplinary readings. Satisfies General Education Requirement: (WC)Grading Restriction: ABC/N grading only.Credit Restriction: Students with credit for ENGL 101 or ENGL 131 or ENGL 198 may not receive credit for ENGL 118.Comment(s): ACT English+composite scores at or above 29 or SAT critical reading+composite scores of 680+1280 required. Students receiving a passing grade below B in ENGL 118 will complete the English Composition requirement by taking ENGL 102. Students receiving a grade of B or above will complete their freshman English requirements by choosing ENGL 102 or a sophomore-level course in the English Department or ENGL 355.

ECE 256
Description: ECE 256 - Computer System Interfaces 3 Credit Hours Introduction to design or implementation,+test of interfaces used in the construction of modern computing systems. Topics covered include memory+I/O devices or component interfaces or real-time operating system concepts or performance analysis,+optimizations. The lectures+lab assignments will cover both hardware+software elements needed to support target applications+interfaces. This includes physical layer+low-level protocol/information-format design+analysis. Other key elements covered in the class include direct memory access or timers or input/output synchronization,+interrupts. Emphasis is placed on hands-on+lab based exercises using an appropriate development system. (RE) Prerequisite(s): ECE 255 with a grade of C or better.

EF 203
Description: EF 203 - Engineering Based Problem Solving 3 Credit Hours The objective is to develop engineering focused critical problem solving skills for undergraduate engineering+business majors. Students are introduced to engineering problems from a systems perspective or allowing students to analyze a range of systems from simple entities to larger more complex systems such as organizations. There are three phases of the critical problem solving skills as exemplified by the DRIVES model. The first phase focuses on defining the right problem. The second phase details a solution based on the concepts of flow or variation,+disruption. The third phase introduces the sustainability of the solution based on the concepts of reliability+the role of culture in design. Alternative solutions will be reviewed from a business perspective. Registration Restriction(s): Sophomore standing.
Prerequisites: 
Corequisites: 

EF 303
Description: EF 303 - Creating Synergies in Business+Engineering Collaborations 3 Credit Hours The objective is to develop the skills+understanding to create effective cross disciplinary engineering+business teams. Students will work to understand the key requirements of projects from both the business+engineering perspective. Additionally or students will be able to apply basic engineering principles in a business context. Scenarios in new product development+operations will be considered. Topics may include identifying needs/key requirements or project management,+sensitivity analysis of solutions from the profit+loss perspective. (RE) Prerequisite(s): EF 203 or consent of instructor.
Prerequisites: EF 203 or consent of instructor
Corequisites:

Description: ECE 336 - Electronic Circuits 3 Credit Hours Multistage transistor amplifier biasing. Gain stages+output stages. Frequency+transient response of open loop linear amplifiers. COSC 425
Description: COSC 425 - Introduction to Machine Learning 3 Credit Hours Machine learning is concerned with computer programs that automatically improve their performance through experience. This course covers the theory+practice of machine learning from a variety of perspectives. We cover topics such as clustering or decision trees or neural network learning or statistical learning methods or Bayesian learning methods or dimension reduction or kernel methods,+reinforcement learning. Programming assignments include implementation+hands-on experiments with various learning algorithms. (RE) Prerequisite(s): ECE 313 or ECE 317 or MATH 323 with a grade of C or better;+MATH 251 or MATH 257 with a grade of C or better.Comment(s): Prior knowledge may satisfy prerequisite with consent of instructor.

ECE 256
Description: ECE 256 - Computer System Interfaces 3 Credit Hours Introduction to design or implementation,+test of interfaces used in the construction of modern computing systems. Topics covered include memory+I/O devices or component interfaces or real-time operating system concepts or performance analysis,+optimizations. The lectures+lab assignments will cover both hardware+software elements needed to support target applications+interfaces. This includes physical layer+low-level protocol/information-format design+analysis. Other key elements covered in the class include direct memory access or timers or input/output synchronization,+interrupts. Emphasis is placed on hands-on+lab based exercises using an appropriate development system. (RE) Prerequisite(s): ECE 255 with a grade of C or better.
Prerequisites: ECE 255 with a grade of C or better
Corequisites: 

ECE 351
Description: ECE 351 - Digital Systems Design 3 Credit Hours Introduction to techniques+strategies for designing digital systems using hardware description languages+industry-standard design tools. Topics include simulation+synthesis of high-level designs or finite state-machine design or digital memory systems or arithmetic circuit design or circuit delay estimation or timing,+power analysis. Laboratory+project activities include the implementation of digital systems using field-programmable gate arrays (FPGAs). (RE) Prerequisite(s): ECE 255 with a grade of C or better.

EF 203
Description: EF 203 - Engineering Based Problem Solving 3 Credit Hours The objective is to develop engineering focused critical problem solving skills for undergraduate engineering+business majors. Students are introduced to engineering problems from a systems perspective or allowing students to analyze a range of systems from simple entities to larger more complex systems such as organizations. There are three phases of the critical problem solving skills as exemplified by the DRIVES model. The first phase focuses on defining the right problem. The second phase details a solution based on the concepts of flow or variation,+disruption. The third phase introduces the sustainability of the solution based on the concepts of reliability+the role of culture in design. Alternative solutions will be reviewed from a business perspective. Registration Restriction(s): Sophomore standing.
Prerequisites: 
Corequisites: 

EF 303
Description: EF 303 - Creating Synergies in Business+Engineering Collaborations 3 Credit Hours The objective is to develop the skills+understanding to create effective cross disciplinary engineering+business teams. Students will work to understand the key requirements of projects from both the business+engineering perspective. Additionally or students will be able to apply basic engineering principles in a business context. Scenarios in new product development+operations will be considered. Topics may include identifying needs/key requirements or project management,+sensitivity analysis of solutions from the profit+loss perspective. (RE) Prerequisite(s): EF 203 or consent of instructor.
Prerequisites: EF 203 or consent of instructor
Corequisites:
